The problem with people not believing in climate change is not because the data is not visceral. It's because the narrative is overblown and it actually doesn't line up with the objective data. People can smell out b.s. a mile away and because of that people don't know where the b.s. and truth line is drawn. So why believe any of it? For crying out loud for 100 years people have been saying that the world is going to end it 10 years., Fair
I love Veritasium but let me understand this video. Sure: anecdotal stories are popular and spreading quick and communicate better. Scientific methods and conclusion hardly can gain that kind of popularity. Let me rephrase this statement with a different metaphor: for an average human being reading Cinderella is much easier and more entertaining than reading even a one page publication from Bohr about spinning electrons. The majority of humans are neither have the brain capacity to deal with Bohr nor the interest or just they are trying to pay their mortgages or survive. It is not a big surprise that easy to understand populist stories trumps over dry data. Same applies to music. It is easier to listen a pop (popular) music then really pay attention to Rachmaninoff. So to the question: why anecdotes trump data? Because one is easy and interesting the other is boring and tedious? Does it mean that an easy read brings more value to society? Soap operas are easy to watch and sadly it is extremely popular. It is not hard to watch 8 seasons of an entertaining show and people do that instead of spending fraction of that time with any mental work (just thinking about another Veritasium video about "Gun" and "Drew"). Yes sometimes anecdotes trump data but it is bad. Why scientific results need to go through on a populist pass? Was any populist voting about how to build a mobile phone launch a rocket build a building or anything? No. Because the majority has and should not have word on it. Because they do not know. It is not their job. For many serious breakthrough results we should do our best to either: avoid the need for a populist pass or create an entertaining story which explains it to a 5 years old. My last metaphor: anecdotes are equivalent to a one page marketing material of a product. Data is the backend. One is not competing with the other but support each other. The user can only read a one pager marketing brochure and make a buying decision and use the product. The backend or engineering will make it useful or not. So my conclusion: we cannot compare anecdotes with data. We need both for success (just because of the consumerism but that is a separate big topic why the hack we even need anecdotes for things should be supported only by data)., Fair
